     <p>
      <b>
       J.R.
      </b>
      "
      <b>
       Johnny
      </b>
      "
      <b>
       Cash
      </b>
      (February 26, 1932 September 12, 2003) was an American
      <a href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter" title="Singer-songwriter">
       singer-songwriter
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">
       actor
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Author" title="Author">
       author
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastfm_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lastfm-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      widely considered one of the most influential
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musicians" title="Musicians">
       musicians
      </a>
      of the 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although primarily remembered as a
      <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">
       country music
      </a>
      icon, his
      <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">
       genre
      </a>
      -spanning songs and sound embraced
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">
       rock and roll
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly">
       rockabilly
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">
       blues
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">
       folk
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">
       gospel
      </a>
      . This crossover appeal won Cash the rare honor of multiple inductions in the
      <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum">
       Country Music
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">
       Rock and Roll
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Gospel Music Hall of Fame">
       Gospel Music
      </a>
      Halls of Fame.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash was known for his deep
      <a href="/wiki/Bass-baritone" title="Bass-baritone">
       bass-baritone
      </a>
      voice,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        a
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dx_dK-0HfHUYC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_xiv.5D_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dx_dK-0HfHUYC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_xiv.5D-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the distinctive sound of his
      <a href="/wiki/The_Tennessee_Three" title="The Tennessee Three">
       Tennessee Three
      </a>
      backing band, a rebelliousness
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dickie_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dickie-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streissguth_profile_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Streissguth_profile-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      coupled with an increasingly somber and humble demeanor,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPareles1994_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPareles1994-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      free prison concerts,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fox-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStreissguth2005_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStreissguth2005-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a trademark look, which earned him the nickname "The Man in Black".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        b
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He traditionally began his concerts with the simple "Hello, I'm Johnny Cash"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        c
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      , followed by his signature "
      <a href="/wiki/Folsom_Prison_Blues" title="Folsom Prison Blues">
       Folsom Prison Blues
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      Much of Cash's music echoed themes of sorrow, moral tribulation and redemption, especially in the later stages of his career.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPareles1994_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPareles1994-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mulligan_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mulligan-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His best-known songs included "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Walk_the_Line" title="I Walk the Line">
       I Walk the Line
      </a>
      ", "
      <a href="/wiki/Folsom_Prison_Blues" title="Folsom Prison Blues">
       Folsom Prison Blues
      </a>
      ", "
      <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire_(song)" title="Ring of Fire (song)">
       Ring of Fire
      </a>
      ", "
      <a href="/wiki/Get_Rhythm" title="Get Rhythm">
       Get Rhythm
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Man_in_Black_(song)" title="Man in Black (song)">
       Man in Black
      </a>
      ". He also recorded humorous numbers like "
      <a href="/wiki/One_Piece_at_a_Time" title="One Piece at a Time">
       One Piece at a Time
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/A_Boy_Named_Sue" title="A Boy Named Sue">
       A Boy Named Sue
      </a>
      "; a duet with his future wife,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/June_Carter" title="June Carter">
       June Carter
      </a>
      , called "
      <a href="/wiki/Jackson_(song)" title="Jackson (song)">
       Jackson
      </a>
      " (followed by many further duets after their marriage); and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_train_songs" title="List of train songs">
       railroad songs
      </a>
      including "
      <a href="/wiki/Hey,_Porter" title="Hey, Porter">
       Hey, Porter
      </a>
      " and "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Island_Line_(song)" title="Rock Island Line (song)">
       Rock Island Line
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cusic_book_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cusic_book-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the last stage of his career, Cash
      <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">
       covered
      </a>
      songs by several late 20th-century rock artists, most notably "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurt_(Johnny_Cash_song)" title="Hurt (Johnny Cash song)">
       Hurt
      </a>
      " by
      <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">
       Nine Inch Nails
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">
       Personal life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Personal life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">
       Early life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Cash was born in
      <a href="/wiki/Kingsland,_Arkansas" title="Kingsland, Arkansas">
       Kingsland, Arkansas
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller2003341_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller2003341-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one of seven
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      children born to Ray Cash (May 13, 1897, Kingsland, Arkansas  December 23, 1985,
      <a href="/wiki/Hendersonville,_Tennessee" title="Hendersonville, Tennessee">
       Hendersonville, Tennessee
      </a>
      ) and Carrie Cloveree (ne Rivers; March 13, 1904,
      <a href="/wiki/Rison,_Arkansas" title="Rison, Arkansas">
       Rison, Arkansas
      </a>
       March 11, 1991, Hendersonville, Tennessee). At birth, he
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was named J. R. Cash. When Cash enlisted in the Air Force, they wouldn't let him use initials as his name, so he started to use the legal name John R. Cash. In 1955, when signing with
      <a href="/wiki/Sun_Records" title="Sun Records">
       Sun Records
      </a>
      , he took Johnny Cash as his stage name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streissguth_profile_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Streissguth_profile-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Cash children were: Roy, Margaret Louise, Jack, J. R., Reba, Joanne and Tommy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His younger brother,
      <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Cash" title="Tommy Cash">
       Tommy Cash
      </a>
      , also became a successful country artist.
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 1935, when Cash was three years old, the family settled in
      <a href="/wiki/Dyess,_Arkansas" title="Dyess, Arkansas">
       Dyess, Arkansas
      </a>
      . He started working in cotton fields at age five, singing along with his family while working. The family farm was flooded on at least two occasions, which later inspired him to write the song "Five Feet High and Rising".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      His family's economic and personal struggles during the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      inspired many of his songs, especially those about other people facing similar difficulties.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash was very close to his older brother, Jack.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In May 1944, Jack was pulled into a whirling
      <a href="/wiki/Head_saw" title="Head saw">
       head saw
      </a>
      in the mill where he worked and was almost cut in two. He suffered for over a week before he died on May 20, 1944, at age 15.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Cash often spoke of the horrible guilt he felt over this incident. According to
      <i>
       Cash: The Autobiography
      </i>
      , his father was away that morning, but he and his mother, and Jack himself, all had premonitions or a sense of foreboding about that day, causing his mother to urge Jack to skip work and go fishing with his brother. Jack insisted on working, as the family needed the money. On his deathbed, Jack said he had visions of heaven and angels. Decades later, Cash spoke of looking forward to meeting his brother in heaven.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streissguth_profile_8-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Streissguth_profile-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's early memories were dominated by
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">
       gospel music
      </a>
      and radio. Taught guitar by his mother and a childhood friend, Cash began playing and writing songs at the age of twelve. When Cash was young, he had a high tenor voice, before becoming a bass-baritone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In high school he sang on a local radio station; decades later he released an album of traditional gospel songs, called
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Mother%27s_Hymn_Book" title="My Mother's Hymn Book">
        My Mother's Hymn Book
       </a>
      </i>
      . He was also significantly influenced by traditional
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ireland" title="Music of Ireland">
       Irish music
      </a>
      that he heard performed weekly by
      <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Day" title="Dennis Day">
       Dennis Day
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Benny" title="Jack Benny">
       Jack Benny
      </a>
      radio program.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGross2006_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGross2006-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash enlisted in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">
       United States Air Force
      </a>
      on July 7, 1950.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basic_training" title="Basic training">
       basic training
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Lackland_Air_Force_Base" title="Lackland Air Force Base">
       Lackland Air Force Base
      </a>
      and technical training at
      <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Air_Force_Base" title="Brooks Air Force Base">
       Brooks Air Force Base
      </a>
      , both in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" title="San Antonio, Texas">
       San Antonio, Texas
      </a>
      , Cash was assigned to the 12th Radio Squadron Mobile of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force_Security_Service" title="U.S. Air Force Security Service">
       U.S. Air Force Security Service
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Landsberg_am_Lech" title="Landsberg am Lech">
       Landsberg
      </a>
      , Germany as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morse_Code" title="Morse Code">
       Morse Code
      </a>
      Intercept Operator for
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">
       Soviet Army
      </a>
      transmissions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was there he created his first band, named "The Landsberg Barbarians".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was the first radio operator to pick up the news of the death of
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
       Joseph Stalin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200340_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200340-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was honorably discharged as a Staff Sergeant on July 3, 1954, and returned to Texas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morsecode_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-morsecode-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages_and_family">
       Marriages and family
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriages and family">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On July 18, 1951, while in Air Force training, Cash met 17-year-old Vivian Liberto at a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roller_skating_rink" title="Roller skating rink">
       roller skating rink
      </a>
      in her native San Antonio. They dated for three weeks, until Cash was deployed to Germany for a three-year tour. During that time, the couple exchanged hundreds of pages of
      <a href="/wiki/Love_letter" title="Love letter">
       love letters
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200443.E2.80.9344_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200443.E2.80.9344-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 7, 1954, one month after his discharge, they were married at St. Ann's Roman Catholic Church in San Antonio. The ceremony was performed by her uncle, Father Vincent Liberto. They had four daughters:
      <a href="/wiki/Rosanne_Cash" title="Rosanne Cash">
       Rosanne
      </a>
      , Kathy, Cindy and Tara. Liberto stated that Cash's drug and alcohol abuse as well as constant touring, affairs with other women, and his close relationship with
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter
      </a>
      led her to file for divorce in 1966.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's career was handled by Saul Holiff, a London, Ontario, promoter and this relationship was the subject of Saul's son's biopic
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/My_Father_and_the_Man_in_Black" title="My Father and the Man in Black">
        My Father and the Man in Black
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1968, 13 years after they first met backstage at the
      <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">
       Grand Ole Opry
      </a>
      , Cash proposed to June Carter, of the famed
      <a href="/wiki/Carter_Family" title="Carter Family">
       Carter Family
      </a>
      , during a live performance in
      <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">
       London, Ontario
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The couple married on March 1, 1968, in
      <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_Kentucky" title="Franklin, Kentucky">
       Franklin, Kentucky
      </a>
      . They had one child together,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Cash" title="John Carter Cash">
       John Carter Cash
      </a>
      , born March 3, 1970. Cash and Carter continued to work together and tour for 35 years until June's death in May 2003. Cash died four months later the same year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Streissguth_profile_8-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Streissguth_profile-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Heritage">
       Heritage
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Heritage">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Cash researched his heritage and found a mix of mostly Scottish and English ancestry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Millar_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Millar-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Memoir1_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Memoir1-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manzoor_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manzoor-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After meeting with the then-
      <a href="/wiki/Laird" title="Laird">
       laird
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Falkland,_Fife" title="Falkland, Fife">
       Falkland, Fife
      </a>
      , Major Michael Crichton-Stuart, Cash traced his family tree to 11th-century
      <a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">
       Fife
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200311_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200311-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr19973_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr19973-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash
      <a href="/wiki/Loch" title="Loch">
       Loch
      </a>
      and other locations in
      <a href="/wiki/Fife" title="Fife">
       Fife
      </a>
      bear the name of his family.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200311_37-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200311-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Career">
       Career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">
       Early career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="513" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg/220px-Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg/330px-Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg/440px-Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_Sun_Records_promotional_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Publicity photo for Sun Records
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1954, Cash and Vivian moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">
       Memphis, Tennessee
      </a>
      , where he sold appliances while studying to be a radio announcer. At night he played with guitarist
      <a href="/wiki/Luther_Perkins" title="Luther Perkins">
       Luther Perkins
      </a>
      and bassist
      <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Grant" title="Marshall Grant">
       Marshall Grant
      </a>
      . Perkins and Grant were known as the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Tennessee_Three" title="The Tennessee Three">
       Tennessee Two
      </a>
      . Cash worked up the courage to visit the
      <a href="/wiki/Sun_Records" title="Sun Records">
       Sun Records
      </a>
      studio, hoping to get a recording contract. After auditioning for
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Phillips" title="Sam Phillips">
       Sam Phillips
      </a>
      , singing mostly gospel songs, Phillips told him that he didn't record gospel music any longer. It was once rumored that Phillips told Cash to "go home and sin, then come back with a song I can sell", although in a 2002 interview Cash denied that Phillips made any such comment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash eventually won over the producer with new songs delivered in his early rockabilly style. In 1955, Cash made his first recordings at Sun, "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hey_Porter" title="Hey Porter">
       Hey Porter
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Cry!_Cry!_Cry!" title="Cry! Cry! Cry!">
       Cry! Cry! Cry!
      </a>
      ", which were released in late June and met with success on the country
      <a href="/wiki/Hit_parade" title="Hit parade">
       hit parade
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 4, 1956,
      <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">
       Elvis Presley
      </a>
      dropped in on Phillips while
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">
       Carl Perkins
      </a>
      was in the studio cutting new tracks, with
      <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lee_Lewis" title="Jerry Lee Lewis">
       Jerry Lee Lewis
      </a>
      backing him on piano. Cash was also in the studio and the four started an
      <a href="/wiki/Impromptu" title="Impromptu">
       impromptu
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Jam_session" title="Jam session">
       jam session
      </a>
      . Phillips left the tapes running and the recordings, almost half of which were gospel songs, survived and have since been released under the title
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Quartet" title="Million Dollar Quartet">
        Million Dollar Quartet
       </a>
      </i>
      . In
      <i>
       Cash: the Autobiography
      </i>
      , Cash wrote that he was the one farthest from the microphone and was singing in a higher pitch to blend in with Elvis.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's next record, "Folsom Prison Blues", made the country Top 5, and "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Walk_the_Line" title="I Walk the Line">
       I Walk the Line
      </a>
      " became No. 1 on the country charts and entered the pop charts Top 20. "
      <a href="/wiki/Home_of_the_Blues" title="Home of the Blues">
       Home of the Blues
      </a>
      " followed, recorded in July 1957. That same year Cash became the first Sun artist to release a
      <a href="/wiki/LP_record" title="LP record">
       long-playing album
      </a>
      . Although he was Sun's most consistently selling and prolific artist at that time, Cash felt constrained by his contract with the small label partly due to the fact that Phillips wasn't keen on Johnny recording gospel, and he was getting only a 3% royalty as opposed to the standard rate of 5%. Presley had already left Sun, and Phillips was focusing most of his attention and promotion on Lewis. The following year, Cash left the label to sign a lucrative offer with
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">
       Columbia Records
      </a>
      , where his single "
      <a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Take_Your_Guns_to_Town" title="Don't Take Your Guns to Town">
       Don't Take Your Guns to Town
      </a>
      " became one of his biggest hits and his second album for Columbia was a collection of gospel songs. However, Cash left behind a sufficient backlog of recordings with Sun that Phillips continued to release new singles and even albums featuring previously unreleased material until as late as 1964, placing Cash in the unusual position of having new releases out on two labels concurrently, with one 1960 release, a cover of "
      <a href="/wiki/Oh_Lonesome_Me" title="Oh Lonesome Me">
       Oh Lonesome Me
      </a>
      " making as high as No. 13 on the C&amp;W charts. (Unlike when
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RCA_Victor" title="RCA Victor">
       RCA Victor
      </a>
      signed Presley and also bought his Sun Records masters, when Cash departed for Columbia, Phillips retained the rights to Cash's Sun masters; Columbia would eventually license some of these recordings for release on compilations after Cash's death.)
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="619" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG/200px-Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG/300px-Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG/400px-Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_and_The_Tennessee_Three_1963.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Tennessee_Three" title="The Tennessee Three">
         The Tennessee Three
        </a>
        with Cash in 1963.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Early in his career, he was given the teasing nickname
      <i>
       The Undertaker
      </i>
      by fellow artists because of his habit of wearing black clothes - though he did so only because they were easier to keep looking clean on long tours.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the early 1960s, Cash toured with the
      <a href="/wiki/Carter_Family" title="Carter Family">
       Carter Family
      </a>
      , which by this time regularly included
      <a href="/wiki/Maybelle_Carter" title="Maybelle Carter">
       Mother Maybelle
      </a>
      's daughters,
      <a href="/wiki/Anita_Carter" title="Anita Carter">
       Anita
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Helen_Carter" title="Helen Carter">
       Helen
      </a>
      . June later recalled admiring him from afar during these tours. In the 1960s, he appeared on
      <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">
       Pete Seeger
      </a>
      's short lived television series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Quest" title="Rainbow Quest">
        Rainbow Quest
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also acted in and wrote and sang the opening theme for a 1961 film entitled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Five_Minutes_to_Live" title="Five Minutes to Live">
        Five Minutes to Live
       </a>
      </i>
      , later re-released as
      <i>
       Door-to-door Maniac
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Outlaw_image">
       Outlaw image
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Outlaw image">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      As his career was taking off in the late 1950s, Cash started drinking heavily and became addicted to
      <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">
       amphetamines
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Barbiturate" title="Barbiturate">
       barbiturates
      </a>
      . For a brief time, he shared an apartment in Nashville with
      <a href="/wiki/Waylon_Jennings" title="Waylon Jennings">
       Waylon Jennings
      </a>
      , who was heavily addicted to amphetamines. Cash used the uppers to stay awake during tours. Friends joked about his "nervousness" and erratic behavior, many ignoring the warning signs of his worsening
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_addiction" title="Drug addiction">
       drug addiction
      </a>
      . In a behind-the-scenes look at
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Johnny_Cash_Show_(TV_series)" title="The Johnny Cash Show (TV series)">
        The Johnny Cash Show
       </a>
      </i>
      , Cash claims to have "tried every drug there was to try."
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Although he was in many ways spiraling out of control, Cash's frenetic creativity was still delivering hits. His rendition of "
      <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire_(song)" title="Ring of Fire (song)">
       Ring of Fire
      </a>
      " was a
      <a href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)" title="Crossover (music)">
       crossover
      </a>
      hit, reaching No. 1 on the country charts and entering the Top 20 on the pop charts. The song was written by
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Merle_Kilgore" title="Merle Kilgore">
       Merle Kilgore
      </a>
      . It was originally performed by June's sister, but the signature
      <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">
       mariachi
      </a>
      -style horn arrangement was provided by Cash,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc10_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pc10-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      who said that it had come to him in a dream. Vivian Liberto claimed a different version of the origins of "Ring of Fire". In her book,
      <i>
       I Walked the Line: My Life with Johnny
      </i>
      , Liberto states that Cash gave Carter the credit for monetary reasons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 1965, his truck caught fire due to an overheated wheel bearing, triggering a forest fire that burnt several hundred acres in
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Padres_National_Forest" title="Los Padres National Forest">
       Los Padres National Forest
      </a>
      in California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When the judge asked Cash why he did it, Cash said, "I didn't do it, my truck did, and it's dead, so you can't question it."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The fire destroyed 508 acres (206ha), burning the foliage off three mountains and driving off 49 of the refuge's 53 endangered
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Condor" title="California Condor">
       condors
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash was unrepentant and claimed, "I don't care about your damn yellow buzzards." The federal government sued him and was awarded $125,172 ($936,741 in 2015 dollars). Cash eventually
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Settlement_(law)" title="Settlement (law)">
       settled
      </a>
      the case and paid $82,001.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He said he was the only person ever sued by the government for starting a forest fire.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Although Cash carefully cultivated a romantic
      <a href="/wiki/Outlaw" title="Outlaw">
       outlaw
      </a>
      image, he never served a prison sentence. Despite landing in jail seven times for
      <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">
       misdemeanors
      </a>
      , each stay lasted only a single night. His most infamous run-in with the law occurred while on tour in 1965, when he was arrested October 4 by a
      <a href="/wiki/Narcotic" title="Narcotic">
       narcotics
      </a>
      squad in
      <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">
       El Paso, Texas
      </a>
      . The officers suspected he was
      <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">
       smuggling
      </a>
      heroin from Mexico, but found instead 688
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dexedrine" title="Dexedrine">
       Dexedrine
      </a>
      capsules and 475
      <a href="/wiki/Meprobamate" title="Meprobamate">
       Equanil
      </a>
      tablets that the singer had hidden inside his guitar case. Because the pills were prescription drugs rather than illegal narcotics, he received a
      <a href="/wiki/Suspended_sentence" title="Suspended sentence">
       suspended sentence
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="695" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg/220px-JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg/330px-JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg/440px-JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JohnnyCashJuneCarterCash1969.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Johnny Cash and his second wife,
        <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
         June Carter
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Cash had also been arrested on May 11, 1965, in
      <a href="/wiki/Starkville,_Mississippi" title="Starkville, Mississippi">
       Starkville, Mississippi
      </a>
      , for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trespassing" title="Trespassing">
       trespassing
      </a>
      late at night onto private property to pick flowers. (This incident gave the spark for the song "Starkville City Jail", which he discussed on his live
      <i>
       At San Quentin
      </i>
      album.)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the mid-1960s, Cash released a number of
      <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">
       concept albums
      </a>
      , including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sings_the_Ballads_of_the_True_West" title="Sings the Ballads of the True West">
        Sings the Ballads of the True West
       </a>
      </i>
      (1965), an experimental double record mixing authentic frontier songs with Cash's spoken narration, and
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitter_Tears" title="Bitter Tears">
        Bitter Tears
       </a>
      </i>
      (1964), with songs highlighting the plight of the Native Americans. His drug addiction was at its worst at this point, and his destructive behavior led to a divorce from his first wife and canceled performances. Nonetheless, he continued to find success and in 1967, Cash's duet with
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter
      </a>
      , "
      <a href="/wiki/Jackson_(song)" title="Jackson (song)">
       Jackson
      </a>
      ", won a
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's final arrest was in 1967 in
      <a href="/wiki/Walker_County,_Georgia" title="Walker County, Georgia">
       Walker County, Georgia
      </a>
      , after being involved in a car accident while carrying a bag of prescription pills. Cash attempted to bribe a local deputy, who turned the money down, and then spent the night in a
      <a href="/wiki/LaFayette,_Georgia" title="LaFayette, Georgia">
       LaFayette, Georgia
      </a>
      , jail. The singer was released after a long talk with Sheriff Ralph Jones, who warned him of his dangerous behavior and wasted potential. Cash credited that experience for saving his life, and he later came back to LaFayette to play a benefit concert that attracted 12,000 people (the city population was less than 9,000 at the time) and raised $75,000 for the high school.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Reflecting on his past in a 1997 interview, Cash noted: I was taking the pills for awhile, and then the pills started taking me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash curtailed his use of drugs for several years in 1968, after a spiritual
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/epiphany" title="wikt:epiphany">
       epiphany
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Nickajack_Cave" title="Nickajack Cave">
       Nickajack Cave
      </a>
      , when he attempted to commit suicide while under the heavy influence of drugs. He descended deeper into the cave, trying to lose himself and "just die", when he passed out on the floor. He reported being exhausted and feeling at the end of his rope when he felt God's presence in his heart and managed to struggle out of the cave (despite the exhaustion) by following a faint light and slight breeze. To him, it was his own rebirth. June,
      <a href="/wiki/Maybelle_Carter" title="Maybelle Carter">
       Maybelle
      </a>
      , and Ezra Carter moved in to Cash's mansion for a month to help him conquer his addiction. Cash proposed onstage to June at a concert at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Gardens" title="London Gardens">
       London Gardens
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">
       London, Ontario
      </a>
      , Canada, on February 22, 1968; the couple married a week later (on March 1) in
      <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_Kentucky" title="Franklin, Kentucky">
       Franklin, Kentucky
      </a>
      . She had agreed to marry Cash after he had "cleaned up".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He rediscovered his Christian faith, taking an "
      <a href="/wiki/Altar_call" title="Altar call">
       altar call
      </a>
      " in Evangel Temple, a small church in the Nashville area, pastored by Reverend Jimmie Rodgers Snow, son of country music legend
      <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">
       Hank Snow
      </a>
      . According to longtime friend
      <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Grant" title="Marshall Grant">
       Marshall Grant
      </a>
      , Cash's 1968 rebirth experience did not result in his completely stopping use of amphetamines. However, beginning in 1970, Cash ended all drug use for a period of seven years. Grant claims that the birth of Cash's son,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Cash" title="John Carter Cash">
       John Carter Cash
      </a>
      , inspired Cash to end his dependence. Cash began using amphetamines again in 1977. By 1983, he was once again addicted, and entered the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betty_Ford_Clinic" title="Betty Ford Clinic">
       Betty Ford Clinic
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Mirage,_California" title="Rancho Mirage, California">
       Rancho Mirage
      </a>
      , California for rehabilitation. Cash managed to stay off drugs for several years, but by 1989, he was dependent again and entered Nashville's Cumberland Heights Alcohol and Drug Treatment Center. In 1992, he entered the Loma Linda Behavioural Medicine Centre in
      <a href="/wiki/Loma_Linda,_California" title="Loma Linda, California">
       Loma Linda, California
      </a>
      , for his final rehabilitation (several months later, his son followed him into this facility for treatment).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grant_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grant-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-John_Carter_Cash_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-John_Carter_Cash-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Folsom_and_other_prison_concerts">
       Folsom and other prison concerts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Folsom and other prison concerts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Cash felt great compassion for prisoners. He began performing concerts at prisons starting in the late 1950s. His first prison concert was on January 1, 1959, at San Quentin State Prison.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cash1958_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cash1958-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These performances led to a pair of highly successful live albums,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/At_Folsom_Prison" title="At Folsom Prison">
        Johnny Cash at Folsom Prison
       </a>
      </i>
      (1968) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/At_San_Quentin" title="At San Quentin">
        Johnny Cash at San Quentin
       </a>
      </i>
      (1969).
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Folsom_State_Prison" title="Folsom State Prison">
       Folsom Prison
      </a>
      record was introduced by a rendition of his "Folsom Prison Blues", while the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Quentin" title="San Quentin">
       San Quentin
      </a>
      record included the crossover hit single "
      <a href="/wiki/A_Boy_Named_Sue" title="A Boy Named Sue">
       A Boy Named Sue
      </a>
      ", a
      <a href="/wiki/Shel_Silverstein" title="Shel Silverstein">
       Shel Silverstein
      </a>
      -penned novelty song that reached No. 1 on the country charts and No. 2 on the U.S.
      <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">
       Top Ten
      </a>
      pop charts. The AM versions of the latter contained profanities which were edited out. The modern CD versions are unedited and thus also longer than the original vinyl albums, though they retain the audience reaction overdubs of the originals.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash performed at the
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%96ster%C3%A5ker_Prison" title="sterker Prison">
       sterker Prison
      </a>
      in Sweden in 1972. The live album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A5_%C3%96ster%C3%A5ker" title="P sterker">
        P sterker
       </a>
      </i>
      ("At sterker") was released in 1973. "San Quentin" was recorded with Cash replacing "San Quentin" with "sterker". In 1976, a further prison concert, this time at Tennessee Prison, was videotaped for TV broadcast and received a belated CD release after Cash's death as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Concert_Behind_Prison_Walls" title="A Concert Behind Prison Walls">
        A Concert Behind Prison Walls
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Activism_for_Native_Americans">
       Activism for Native Americans
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Activism for Native Americans">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1965, Cash and his wife, June Carter Cash, appeared on
      <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">
       Pete Seeger
      </a>
      s TV show,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Quest" title="Rainbow Quest">
        Rainbow Quest
       </a>
      </i>
      , on which Cash explained his start as an activist for
      <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
       Native Americans
      </a>
      :
     </p>
     <p>
      In 57 I wrote a song called 'Old Apache Squaw' and then forgot the so-called Indian protest for a while, but nobody else seemed to speak up with any volume of voice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Columbia, the label for which Cash was recording then, was opposed to putting the song on his next album, considering it "too radical for the public."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash singing songs of Indian tragedy and settler violence went radically against the mainstream of country music in the 1950s, which was dominated by the image of the righteous cowboy who simply makes the natives soil his own.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1964, coming off of the chart success that his previous album 
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Walk_The_Line" title="I Walk The Line">
       I Walk The Line
      </a>
       had been, he recorded the aforementioned album
      <a href="/wiki/Bitter_Tears:_Ballads_of_the_American_Indian" title="Bitter Tears: Ballads of the American Indian">
       Bitter Tears: Ballads of the American Indian
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The album featured stories of a multitude of native peoples, mostly of their violent oppression by white settlers: The Pima (The Ballad of Ira Hayes), Navajo (Navajo), Apache (Apache Tears), Lakota (Big Foot), Seneca (As Long as the Grass Shall Grow), and Cherokee (Talking Leaves). Cash wrote three of the songs himself and one with the help of
      <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Horton" title="Johnny Horton">
       Johnny Horton
      </a>
      , but the majority of the protest songs were written by folk artist
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_LaFarge" title="Peter LaFarge">
       Peter LaFarge
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Writers_Credits_to_Bitter_Tears_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Writers_Credits_to_Bitter_Tears-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (son of activist and Pulitzer prizewinner
      <a href="/wiki/Oliver_La_Farge" title="Oliver La Farge">
       Oliver La Farge
      </a>
      ), whom Cash met in New York in the 1960s and whom he admired for his activism.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album's single, The Ballad of Ira Hayes, was neglected by non-political radio at the time, and the record label denied it any promotion due to its provocative protesting and thus unappealing nature.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash faced resistance and was even urged by an editor of a country-music magazine to leave the
      <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association" title="Country Music Association">
       Country Music Association
      </a>
      : You and your crowd are just too intelligent to associate with plain country folks, country artists and country DJs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-auto-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In reaction, on August 22, 1964, the singer posted a letter as an advertisement in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Magazine" title="Billboard Magazine">
       Billboard Magazine
      </a>
      , calling the record industry cowardly. D.J.s  station managers  owners...where are your guts? he demands. I had to fight back when I realized that so many stations are afraid of Ira Hayes. Just one question: WHY??? He concludes the letter, Ira Hayes is strong medicine.... So is Rochester, Harlem, Birmingham and Vietnam.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash kept promoting the song himself and used his influence on radio disc jockeys he knew eventually to make the song climb to number three on the
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts#Country" title="Billboard charts">
       country charts
      </a>
      , while the album rose to number two on the
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts#Albums" title="Billboard charts">
       album charts
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_64-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-auto-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="446" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg/200px-JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg/300px-JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg/400px-JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JohnnyCashHouse1969.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cash in 1969.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Later, on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Johnny_Cash_Show" title="The Johnny Cash Show">
       The Johnny Cash Show
      </a>
      , he continued telling stories of Native-American plight, both in song and through short films, such as the history of the
      <a href="/wiki/Trail_of_Tears" title="Trail of Tears">
       Trail of Tears
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1966, in response to his activism, the singer was adopted by the Seneca Nations Turtle Clan. He performed benefits in 1968 at the Rosebud Reservation, close to the historical landmark of the battle at
      <a href="/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Massacre" title="Wounded Knee Massacre">
       Wounded Knee
      </a>
      , to raise money to help build a school. He also played at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D-Q_University" title="D-Q University">
       D-Q University
      </a>
      in the 1980s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22The_Man_in_Black.22">
       "The Man in Black"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title='Edit section: "The Man in Black"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="348" data-file-width="499" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg/250px-Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg/375px-Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash-Nixon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cash advocated
        <a href="/wiki/Prison_reform" title="Prison reform">
         prison reform
        </a>
        at his July 1972 meeting with United States President
        <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
         Richard Nixon
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From 1969 to 1971, Cash starred in his own television show,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Johnny_Cash_Show_(TV_series)" title="The Johnny Cash Show (TV series)">
        The Johnny Cash Show
       </a>
      </i>
      , on the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
       ABC
      </a>
      network.
      <a href="/wiki/The_Statler_Brothers" title="The Statler Brothers">
       The Statler Brothers
      </a>
      opened up for him in every episode; the Carter Family and rockabilly legend
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">
       Carl Perkins
      </a>
      were also part of the regular show entourage. Cash also enjoyed booking mainstream performers as guests; including
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Young" title="Neil Young">
       Neil Young
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">
       Louis Armstrong
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond" title="Neil Diamond">
       Neil Diamond
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Rogers_and_The_First_Edition" title="Kenny Rogers and The First Edition">
       Kenny Rogers and The First Edition
      </a>
      (who appeared a record four times),
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">
       Ray Charles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Roger_Miller" title="Roger Miller">
       Roger Miller
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Derek_and_the_Dominos" title="Derek and the Dominos">
       Derek and the Dominos
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      . During the same period, he contributed the title song and other songs to the film
      <i>
       Little Fauss and Big Halsey
      </i>
      , which starred
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Redford" title="Robert Redford">
       Robert Redford
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Pollard" title="Michael J. Pollard">
       Michael J. Pollard
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Hutton" title="Lauren Hutton">
       Lauren Hutton
      </a>
      . The title song,
      <i>
       The Ballad of Little Fauss and Big Halsey
      </i>
      , written by Carl Perkins, was nominated for a Golden Globe award.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash had met with Dylan in the mid-1960s and became closer friends when they were neighbors in the late 1960s in
      <a href="/wiki/Woodstock,_New_York" title="Woodstock, New York">
       Woodstock, New York
      </a>
      . Cash was enthusiastic about reintroducing the reclusive Dylan to his audience. Cash sang a duet with Dylan on Dylan's country album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Skyline" title="Nashville Skyline">
        Nashville Skyline
       </a>
      </i>
      and also wrote the album's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy" title="Grammy">
       Grammy
      </a>
      -winning
      <a href="/wiki/Liner_notes" title="Liner notes">
       liner notes
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Another artist who received a major career boost from
      <i>
       The Johnny Cash Show
      </i>
      was
      <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">
       Kris Kristofferson
      </a>
      , who was beginning to make a name for himself as a singer/songwriter. During a live performance of Kristofferson's "
      <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mornin%27_Comin%27_Down" title="Sunday Mornin' Comin' Down">
       Sunday Mornin' Comin' Down
      </a>
      ", Cash refused to change the lyrics to suit network executives, singing the song with its references to
      <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">
       marijuana
      </a>
      intact:
     </p>
     <div class="poem">
      <p>
       On a Sunday morning sidewalk
       <br/>
       I'm wishin', Lord, that I was stoned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         67
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </div>
     <p>
      By the early 1970s, he had crystallized his public image as "The Man in Black". He regularly performed dressed all in black, wearing a long black knee-length coat. This outfit stood in contrast to the costumes worn by most of the major country acts in his day:
      <a href="/wiki/Rhinestone" title="Rhinestone">
       rhinestone
      </a>
      suits and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cowboy_boots" title="Cowboy boots">
       cowboy boots
      </a>
      . In 1971, Cash wrote the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Man_in_Black_(song)" title="Man in Black (song)">
       Man in Black
      </a>
      ", to help explain his dress code:
     </p>
     <div class="poem">
      <p>
       We're doing mighty fine I do suppose
       <br/>
       In our streak of lightning cars and fancy clothes
       <br/>
       But just so we're reminded of the ones who are held back
       <br/>
       Up front there ought to be a man in black.
      </p>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1230" data-file-width="1908" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg/250px-Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg/375px-Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg/500px-Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johnny-Cash_1972.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cash performing in
        <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">
         Bremen
        </a>
        , Northern Germany, in September 1972
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      He wore black on behalf of the
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">
       poor
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">
       hungry
      </a>
      , on behalf of "the prisoner who has long paid for his crime", and on behalf of those who have been betrayed by age or drugs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr199785.E2.80.9386_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr199785.E2.80.9386-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "And", Cash added, "with the
      <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
       Vietnam War
      </a>
      as painful in my mind as it was in most other Americans', I wore it 'in mournin' for the lives that could have been.'... Apart from the Vietnam War being over, I don't see much reason to change my position... The old are still neglected, the poor are still poor, the young are still dying before their time, and we're not making many moves to make things right. There's still plenty of darkness to carry off."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr199785.E2.80.9386_71-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr199785.E2.80.9386-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One_piece_at_a_time.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1561" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/One_piece_at_a_time.jpg/200px-One_piece_at_a_time.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/One_piece_at_a_time.jpg/300px-One_piece_at_a_time.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/One_piece_at_a_time.jpg/400px-One_piece_at_a_time.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:One_piece_at_a_time.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cash in the "one piece at a time" Cadillac.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      He and his band had initially worn black shirts because that was the only matching color they had among their various outfits. He wore other colors on stage early in his career, but he claimed to like wearing black both on and off stage. He stated that, political reasons aside, he simply liked black as his on-stage color.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The outdated
      <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Uniforms of the United States Navy">
       US Navy's winter blue uniform
      </a>
      used to be referred to by sailors as "Johnny Cashes", as the uniform's shirt, tie, and trousers are solid black.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the mid-1970s, Cash's popularity and number of hit songs began to decline. He made commercials for
      <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">
       Amoco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/STP_(motor_oil_company)" title="STP (motor oil company)">
       STP
      </a>
      , an unpopular enterprise in an era in which oil companies made high profits while consumers suffered through high gasoline prices and shortages. However, his first autobiography,
      <i>
       Man in Black
      </i>
      , was published in 1975 and sold 1.3million copies. A second,
      <i>
       Cash: The Autobiography
      </i>
      , appeared in 1997.
     </p>
     <p>
      His friendship with
      <a href="/wiki/Billy_Graham" title="Billy Graham">
       Billy Graham
      </a>
      led to the production of a film about the life of Jesus,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gospel_Road" title="The Gospel Road">
        The Gospel Road
       </a>
      </i>
      , which Cash co-wrote and narrated. Cash and June Carter Cash appeared several times on the
      <i>
       Billy Graham Crusade
      </i>
      TV specials, and Cash continued to include gospel and religious songs on many of his albums, though Columbia declined to release
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Believer_Sings_the_Truth" title="A Believer Sings the Truth">
        A Believer Sings the Truth
       </a>
      </i>
      , a gospel double-LP Cash recorded in 1979 and which ended up being released on an independent label even with Cash still under contract to Columbia. On November 22, 1974, CBS ran his one-hour TV special entitled "Riding The Rails", a musical history of trains.
     </p>
     <p>
      He continued to appear on television, hosting an annual Christmas special on
      <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
       CBS
      </a>
      throughout the 1970s. Later television appearances included a starring role in an episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Columbo_episodes#Season_3" title="List of Columbo episodes">
        Columbo
       </a>
      </i>
      , entitled "Swan Song". He and June appeared in an episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Little_House_on_the_Prairie_(TV_series)" title="Little House on the Prairie (TV series)">
        Little House on the Prairie
       </a>
      </i>
      , entitled "The Collection". He gave a performance as
      <a href="/wiki/John_Brown_(abolitionist)" title="John Brown (abolitionist)">
       John Brown
      </a>
      in the 1985
      <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
       American Civil War
      </a>
      television mini-series
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_and_South_(TV_miniseries)" title="North and South (TV miniseries)">
        North and South
       </a>
      </i>
      . Johnny and June also appeared in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dr._Quinn,_Medicine_Woman" title="Dr. Quinn, Medicine Woman">
        Dr. Quinn, Medicine Woman
       </a>
      </i>
      in recurring roles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He was friendly with every US President starting with
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
       Richard Nixon
      </a>
      . He was closest to
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">
       Jimmy Carter
      </a>
      , with whom he became close friends and who was a distant cousin of his wife,
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter Cash
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
