        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      When invited to perform at the
      <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
       White House
      </a>
      for the first time in 1970,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Richard Nixon's office requested that he play "
      <a href="/wiki/Okie_from_Muskogee_(song)" title="Okie from Muskogee (song)">
       Okie from Muskogee
      </a>
      " (a satirical
      <a href="/wiki/Merle_Haggard" title="Merle Haggard">
       Merle Haggard
      </a>
      song about people who despised youthful drug users and war protesters), "Welfare Cadillac" (a Guy Drake song which denies the integrity of welfare recipients), and "A Boy Named Sue." Cash declined to play the first two and instead selected other songs, including "The Ballad of
      <a href="/wiki/Ira_Hayes" title="Ira Hayes">
       Ira Hayes
      </a>
      " (about a brave
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
       Native American
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      veteran who was mistreated upon his return to
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">
       Arizona
      </a>
      ), and his own compositions, "
      <a href="/wiki/What_Is_Truth_(song)" title="What Is Truth (song)">
       What Is Truth
      </a>
      " and "Man in Black". Cash wrote that the reasons for denying Nixon's song choices were not knowing them and having fairly short notice to rehearse them, rather than any political reason.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997_22-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr1997-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      However, Cash added, even if Nixon's office had given Cash enough time to learn and rehearse the songs, their choice of pieces that conveyed "
      <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">
       antihippie
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">
       antiblack
      </a>
      " sentiments might have backfired.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr2003212_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr2003212-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In his remarks when introducing Cash, Nixon joked that one thing he'd learned about the singer was one didn't tell him what to sing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Highwaymen_and_Departure_from_Columbia_Records">
       Highwaymen and Departure from Columbia Records
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Highwaymen and Departure from Columbia Records">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Highwaymen.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="350" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Highwaymen.jpg/200px-Highwaymen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Highwaymen.jpg/300px-Highwaymen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7f/Highwaymen.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Highwaymen.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Highwaymen_(country_supergroup)" title="The Highwaymen (country supergroup)">
         The Highwaymen
        </a>
        members
        <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">
         Kris Kristofferson
        </a>
        , Johnny Cash,
        <a href="/wiki/Waylon_Jennings" title="Waylon Jennings">
         Waylon Jennings
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">
         Willie Nelson
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1980, Cash became the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Country Music Hall of Fame">
       Country Music Hall of Fame's
      </a>
      youngest living inductee at age 48, but during the 1980s his records failed to make a major impact on the country charts, although he continued to tour successfully. In the mid-1980s, he recorded and toured with
      <a href="/wiki/Waylon_Jennings" title="Waylon Jennings">
       Waylon Jennings
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">
       Willie Nelson
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">
       Kris Kristofferson
      </a>
      as
      <a href="/wiki/The_Highwaymen_(country_supergroup)" title="The Highwaymen (country supergroup)">
       The Highwaymen
      </a>
      , making three hit albums which were released beginning with the originally titled "Highwaymen" in 1985, followed by "Highwaymen 2" in 1990, and concluding with "Highwaymen The Road Goes on forever" in 1995. Of the group's four members, Cash was the only non-Texan.
     </p>
     <p>
      During that period, Cash appeared in a number of television films. In 1981, he starred in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Pride_of_Jesse_Hallam" title="The Pride of Jesse Hallam">
        The Pride of Jesse Hallam
       </a>
      </i>
      , winning fine reviews for a film that called attention to adult
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illiteracy" title="Illiteracy">
       illiteracy
      </a>
      . In the same year, Cash appeared as a "very special guest star" in an episode of the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muppet_Show" title="Muppet Show">
        Muppet Show
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 1983, he appeared as a heroic sheriff in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Murder_in_Coweta_County" title="Murder in Coweta County">
        Murder in Coweta County
       </a>
      </i>
      , based on a real-life Georgia murder case, which co-starred
      <a href="/wiki/Andy_Griffith" title="Andy Griffith">
       Andy Griffith
      </a>
      as his nemesis. Cash had tried for years to make the film, for which he won acclaim.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash relapsed into addiction after being administered painkillers for a serious abdominal injury in 1983 caused by an unusual incident in which he was kicked and wounded by an ostrich he kept on his farm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At a hospital visit in 1988, this time to watch over Waylon Jennings (who was recovering from a heart attack), Jennings suggested that Cash have himself checked into the hospital for his own heart condition. Doctors recommended preventive heart surgery, and Cash underwent
      <a href="/wiki/Coronary_artery_bypass_surgery" title="Coronary artery bypass surgery">
       double bypass surgery
      </a>
      in the same hospital. Both recovered, although Cash refused to use any prescription painkillers, fearing a relapse into dependency. Cash later claimed that during his operation, he had what is called a "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near_death_experience" title="Near death experience">
       near death experience
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's recording career and his general relationship with the Nashville establishment were at an all-time low in the 1980s. He realized that his record label of nearly 30 years, Columbia, was growing indifferent to him and was not properly marketing him (he was "invisible" during that time, as he said in his autobiography).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1984, Cash released a self-parody recording titled "Chicken in Black," about Cash's brain being transplanted into a chicken and Cash receiving a bank robber's brain in return. Biographer Robert Hilburn, in the 2013-published
      <i>
       Johnny Cash: The Life
      </i>
      disputes the claim made that Cash chose to record an intentionally poor song in protest of Columbia's treatment of him. On the contrary, Hilburn writes, it was Columbia that presented Cash with the song, which Cash - who had previously scored major chart hits with comedic material such as "A Boy Named Sue" and "One Piece at a Time" - accepted enthusiastically, performing the song live on stage and filming a comedic
      <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">
       music video
      </a>
      in which he dresses up in a superhero-like bank robber costume. According to Hilburn, Cash's enthusiasm for the song waned after
      <a href="/wiki/Waylon_Jennings" title="Waylon Jennings">
       Waylon Jennings
      </a>
      told Cash he looked "like a buffoon" in the music video (which was showcased during Cash's 1984 Christmas TV special), and Cash subsequently demanded that Columbia withdraw the music video from broadcast and recall the single from storesinterrupting its bona fide chart successand termed the venture "a fiasco.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1981 and 1984, he recorded several sessions with famed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Countrypolitan" title="Countrypolitan">
       countrypolitan
      </a>
      producer
      <a href="/wiki/Billy_Sherrill" title="Billy Sherrill">
       Billy Sherrill
      </a>
      (who also produced "Chicken in Black") which were shelved; they would be released by Columbia's sister label,
      <a href="/wiki/Legacy_Recordings" title="Legacy Recordings">
       Legacy Recordings
      </a>
      , in 2014 as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Out_Among_the_Stars" title="Out Among the Stars">
        Out Among the Stars
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ats_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ats-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Around this time, Cash also recorded
      <a href="/wiki/Believe_in_Him" title="Believe in Him">
       an album of gospel recordings
      </a>
      that ended up being released by another label around the time of his departure from Columbia (this due to Columbia closing down its Priority Records division that was to have released the recordings).
     </p>
     <p>
      After more unsuccessful recordings were released in 1984-85, Cash left Columbia (At least as a solo artist; he continued to record for Columbia on non-solo projects until as late as 1990, recording a duets album with
      <a href="/wiki/Waylon_Jennings" title="Waylon Jennings">
       Waylon Jennings
      </a>
      and two albums as a member of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Highwaymen" title="The Highwaymen">
       The Highwaymen
      </a>
      .)
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1986, Cash returned to Sun Studios in Memphis to team up with
      <a href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison" title="Roy Orbison">
       Roy Orbison
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lee_Lewis" title="Jerry Lee Lewis">
       Jerry Lee Lewis
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">
       Carl Perkins
      </a>
      to create the album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Class_of_%2755" title="Class of '55">
        Class of '55
       </a>
      </i>
      ; according to Hilburn, Columbia still had Cash under contract at the time, so special arrangements had to be made to allow him to participate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also in 1986, Cash published his only novel,
      <i>
       Man in White
      </i>
      , a book about
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" title="Paul of Tarsus">
       Saul
      </a>
      and his conversion to become the Apostle Paul. He recorded
      <i>
       Johnny Cash Reads The Complete
       <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
        New Testament
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1990.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="American_Recordings">
       American Recordings
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: American Recordings">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="2874" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg/220px-Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg/330px-Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg/440px-Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johnny_Cash_sings_a_duet_with_a_Navy_lieutenant.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Johnny Cash sings a duet with a Navy lieutenant c. 1987
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">
       Columbia Records
      </a>
      dropped Cash from his recording contract, he had a short and unsuccessful stint with
      <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Records" title="Mercury Records">
       Mercury Records
      </a>
      from 1987 to 1991 (see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash_discography#Mercury_Records" title="Johnny Cash discography">
       Johnny Cash discography
      </a>
      ). During this time, he recorded an album of new versions of some of his best-known Sun and Columbia hits, as well as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Water_from_the_Wells_of_Home" title="Water from the Wells of Home">
        Water from the Wells of Home
       </a>
      </i>
      , a duets album that paired him with, among others, his children
      <a href="/wiki/Rosanne_Cash" title="Rosanne Cash">
       Rosanne Cash
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Cash" title="John Carter Cash">
       John Carter Cash
      </a>
      , as well as
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">
       Paul McCartney
      </a>
      <i>
       .
      </i>
     </p>
     <p>
      His career was rejuvenated in the 1990s, leading to popularity with an audience which was not traditionally considered interested in country music. In 1991, he sang a version of "Man in Black" for the
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_punk" title="Christian punk">
       Christian punk
      </a>
      band
      <a href="/wiki/One_Bad_Pig" title="One Bad Pig">
       One Bad Pig
      </a>
      's album
      <i>
       I Scream Sunday
      </i>
      . In 1993, he sang "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Wanderer_(U2_song)" title="The Wanderer (U2 song)">
       The Wanderer
      </a>
      " on
      <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">
       U2
      </a>
      's album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Zooropa" title="Zooropa">
        Zooropa
       </a>
      </i>
      . Although no longer sought after by major labels, he was offered a contract with producer
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">
       Rick Rubin
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Recordings_(US)" title="American Recordings (US)">
       American Recordings
      </a>
      label, which had recently been rebranded from Def American, under which name it was better known for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rap_music" title="Rap music">
       rap
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">
       hard rock
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Under Rubin's supervision, he recorded
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_Recordings_(album)" title="American Recordings (album)">
        American Recordings
       </a>
      </i>
      (1994) in his living room, accompanied only by his Martin Dreadnought guitar one of many Cash played throughout his career.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album featured covers of contemporary artists selected by Rubin and had a great deal of critical and commercial success, winning a Grammy for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Contemporary_Folk_Album" title="Best Contemporary Folk Album">
       Best Contemporary Folk Album
      </a>
      . Cash wrote that his reception at the 1994
      <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">
       Glastonbury Festival
      </a>
      was one of the highlights of his career. This was the beginning of a decade of music industry accolades and commercial success. He teamed up with
      <a href="/wiki/Brooks_%26_Dunn" title="Brooks &amp; Dunn">
       Brooks &amp; Dunn
      </a>
      to contribute "
      <a href="/wiki/Folsom_Prison_Blues" title="Folsom Prison Blues">
       Folsom Prison Blues
      </a>
      " to the AIDS benefit album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_%2B_Country" title="Red Hot + Country">
        Red Hot + Country
       </a>
      </i>
      produced by the
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Organization" title="Red Hot Organization">
       Red Hot Organization
      </a>
      . On the same album, he performed the
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      favorite "
      <a href="/wiki/Forever_Young_(Bob_Dylan_song)" title="Forever Young (Bob Dylan song)">
       Forever Young
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash and his wife appeared on a number of episodes of the television series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dr._Quinn,_Medicine_Woman" title="Dr. Quinn, Medicine Woman">
        Dr. Quinn, Medicine Woman
       </a>
      </i>
      . He also lent his voice for a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameo_role" title="Cameo role">
       cameo role
      </a>
      in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">
        The Simpsons
       </a>
      </i>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/El_Viaje_Misterioso_de_Nuestro_Jomer_(The_Mysterious_Voyage_of_Homer)" title="El Viaje Misterioso de Nuestro Jomer (The Mysterious Voyage of Homer)">
       El Viaje Misterioso de Nuestro Jomer (The Mysterious Voyage of Homer)
      </a>
      ", as the "Space Coyote" that guides
      <a href="/wiki/Homer_Simpson" title="Homer Simpson">
       Homer Simpson
      </a>
      on a spiritual quest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1996, Cash enlisted the accompaniment of
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Petty_and_the_Heartbreakers" title="Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers">
       Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers
      </a>
      and released
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Unchained_(Johnny_Cash_album)" title="Unchained (Johnny Cash album)">
        Unchained
       </a>
      </i>
      (also known as
      <i>
       American Recordings II
      </i>
      ), which won the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Country_Album" title="Best Country Album">
       Best Country Album
      </a>
      Grammy in 1998. The album was produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">
       Rick Rubin
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Massy" title="Sylvia Massy">
       Sylvia Massy
      </a>
      engineering and mixing. A majority of "Unchained" was recorded at
      <a href="/wiki/Sound_City_Studios" title="Sound City Studios">
       Sound City Studios
      </a>
      and featured guest appearances by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lindsay_Buckingham" title="Lindsay Buckingham">
       Lindsay Buckingham
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mick_Fleetwood" title="Mick Fleetwood">
       Mick Fleetwood
      </a>
      and Marty Stewart. Believing he did not explain enough of himself in his 1975 autobiography
      <i>
       Man in Black
      </i>
      , he wrote
      <i>
       Cash: The Autobiography
      </i>
      in 1997.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Last_years">
       Last years
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Last years">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cashcartergrab.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="800" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cashcartergrab.jpg/220px-Cashcartergrab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cashcartergrab.jpg/330px-Cashcartergrab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cashcartergrab.jpg/440px-Cashcartergrab.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cashcartergrab.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cash's original grave (top) and the Cash/Carter memorial
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1997, Cash was diagnosed with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neurodegenerative" title="Neurodegenerative">
       neurodegenerative
      </a>
      disease
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shy-Drager_syndrome" title="Shy-Drager syndrome">
       Shy-Drager syndrome
      </a>
      , a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Multiple_system_atrophy" title="Multiple system atrophy">
       multiple system atrophy
      </a>
      ; according to biographer Robert Hilburn, the disease was originally misdiagnosed as
      <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease">
       Parkinson's disease
      </a>
      , and Cash even announced to a concert audience that he had Parkinson's during a show in
      <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">
       Flint, Michigan
      </a>
      on Oct. 25, 1997 after he nearly collapsed on stage; soon after his diagnosis was changed to Shy-Drager and Cash was told he had approximately 18 months to live.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The diagnosis was later again altered to
      <a href="/wiki/Dysautonomia" title="Dysautonomia">
       autonomic neuropathy
      </a>
      associated with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">
       diabetes
      </a>
      . The illness forced Cash to curtail his touring. He was hospitalized in 1998 with severe
      <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">
       pneumonia
      </a>
      , which damaged his lungs. The albums
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_III:_Solitary_Man" title="American III: Solitary Man">
        American III: Solitary Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (2000) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_IV:_The_Man_Comes_Around" title="American IV: The Man Comes Around">
        American IV: The Man Comes Around
       </a>
      </i>
      (2002) contained Cash's response to his illness in the form of songs of a slightly more somber tone than the first two American albums. The video that was released for "
      <a href="/wiki/Hurt_(Nine_Inch_Nails_song)" title="Hurt (Nine Inch Nails song)">
       Hurt
      </a>
      ", a cover of the song by
      <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">
       Nine Inch Nails
      </a>
      , fits Cash's view of his past and feelings of regret. The video for the song, from
      <i>
       American IV
      </i>
      , is now generally recognized as "his
      <a href="/wiki/Epitaph" title="Epitaph">
       epitaph
      </a>
      ,"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      and received particular critical and popular acclaim.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter Cash
      </a>
      died on May 15, 2003, at the age of 73. June had told Cash to keep working, so he continued to record, completing 60 more songs in the last four months of his life, and even performed a couple of surprise shows at the
      <a href="/wiki/Carter_Family_Fold" title="Carter Family Fold">
       Carter Family Fold
      </a>
      outside
      <a href="/wiki/Bristol,_Virginia" title="Bristol, Virginia">
       Bristol, Virginia
      </a>
      . At the July 5, 2003, concert (his last public performance), before singing "
      <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire_(song)" title="Ring of Fire (song)">
       Ring of Fire
      </a>
      ", Cash read a statement about his late wife that he had written shortly before taking the stage:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       The spirit of June Carter overshadows me tonight with the love she had for me and the love I have for her. We connect somewhere between here and heaven. She came down for a short visit, I guess, from heaven to visit with me tonight to give me courage and inspiration like she always has.
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Cash continued to record until shortly before his death. His final recordings were made on August 21, 2003 and consisted of "Like the 309," which would appear on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_V:_A_Hundred_Highways" title="American V: A Hundred Highways">
        American V: A Hundred Highways
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2006, and the final song he completed, "Engine 143," which was recorded for his son John Carter Cash for a planned Carter Family tribute album.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Death">
       Death
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Death">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      While hospitalized at Baptist Hospital in Nashville, Cash died of complications from diabetes at approximately 2:00a.m. CT on September 12, 2003, aged 71less than four months after his wife. It was suggested that Johnny's health worsened due to a
      <a href="/wiki/Broken_heart" title="Broken heart">
       broken heart
      </a>
      over June's death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was buried next to his wife in
      <a href="/wiki/Hendersonville_Memory_Gardens" title="Hendersonville Memory Gardens">
       Hendersonville Memory Gardens
      </a>
      near his home in
      <a href="/wiki/Hendersonville,_Tennessee" title="Hendersonville, Tennessee">
       Hendersonville, Tennessee
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 2005, Cash's lakeside home on Caudill Drive in Hendersonville was put up for sale by his estate. In January 2006, the house was sold to
      <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">
       Bee Gees
      </a>
      vocalist
      <a href="/wiki/Barry_Gibb" title="Barry Gibb">
       Barry Gibb
      </a>
      and wife Linda and titled to their Florida limited liability company for $2.3million. The listing agent was Cash's younger brother,
      <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Cash" title="Tommy Cash">
       Tommy
      </a>
      . On April 10, 2007, during a major restoration of the property by the new owner, Cash's home was accidentally destroyed in a spontaneous combustion-ignited fire caused by workers using linseed oil products.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One of Cash's final collaborations with producer
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">
       Rick Rubin
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_V:_A_Hundred_Highways" title="American V: A Hundred Highways">
        American V: A Hundred Highways
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released posthumously on July 4, 2006. The album debuted in the No.1 position on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      Top 200 album chart for the week ending July 22, 2006. On February 23, 2010, three days before what would have been Cash's 78th birthday, the Cash Family,
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">
       Rick Rubin
      </a>
      , and Lost Highway Records released his second posthumous record, titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_VI:_Ain%27t_No_Grave" title="American VI: Ain't No Grave">
        American VI: Ain't No Grave
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_beliefs">
       Religious beliefs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religious beliefs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Cash was raised by his parents in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist" title="Southern Baptist">
       Southern Baptist
      </a>
      faith tradition. He was baptized in 1944 in the Tyronza River as a member of the Central Baptist Church of
      <a href="/wiki/Dyess,_Arkansas" title="Dyess, Arkansas">
       Dyess, Arkansas
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Man_In_Black_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Man_In_Black-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A troubled but devout Christian,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClapp2008.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D0qIWgaPi9E8C.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_xvi.5D_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClapp2008.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D0qIWgaPi9E8C.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_xvi.5D-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Cash has been characterized as a "lens through which to view American contradictions and challenges."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        d
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClapp2008xviii_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClapp2008xviii-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DNZDEbEHKMPsC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_227.5D_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DNZDEbEHKMPsC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_227.5D-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_studies" title="Biblical studies">
       biblical scholar
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lastfm_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-lastfm-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stoudt_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stoudt-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRX_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PRX-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      he penned a
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_novel" title="Christian novel">
       Christian novel
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       Man in White
      </i>
      , and in the introduction Cash writes about a reporter who, interested in Cash's religious beliefs, questions whether the book is written from a Baptist, Catholic, or Jewish perspective. Cash denies an answer to the book's view and his own, and replies, "I'm a Christian. Don't put me in another box."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECash2008_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECash2008-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2012)">
          pageneeded
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCNews_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBCNews-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He made a spoken word recording of the entire
      <a href="/wiki/New_King_James_Version" title="New King James Version">
       New King James Version
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
       New Testament
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rivkin_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rivkin-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Morris-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash declared he was "the biggest sinner of them all", and viewed himself overall as a complicated and contradictory man.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003xx.E2.80.93xxi_100-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbanski2003xx.E2.80.93xxi-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urbanski_black_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urbanski_black-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        e
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Accordingly,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urbanski2_106-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urbanski2-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        f
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash is said to have "contained multitudes", and has been deemed "the philosopher-prince of American country music".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huss_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Huss-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Court_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Open_Court-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash is credited with converting actor and singer
      <a href="/wiki/John_Schneider_(screen_actor)" title="John Schneider (screen actor)">
       John Schneider
      </a>
      to Christianity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">
       Legacy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Legacy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Cash's rebellious image and often anti-authoritarian stance have been credited by some with influencing
      <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">
       punk rock
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash's daughter
      <a href="/wiki/Rosanne_Cash" title="Rosanne Cash">
       Rosanne
      </a>
      (by first wife
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vivian_Liberto" title="Vivian Liberto">
       Vivian Liberto
      </a>
      ) and his son
      <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_Cash" title="John Carter Cash">
       John Carter Cash
      </a>
      (by
      <a href="/wiki/June_Carter_Cash" title="June Carter Cash">
       June Carter Cash
      </a>
      ) are notable musicians in their own right.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cash nurtured and defended artists (such as
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc10_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pc10-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ) on the fringes of what was acceptable in country music even while serving as the country music establishment's most visible symbol. At an all-star concert which aired in 1999 on
      <a href="/wiki/TNT_(TV_channel)" title="TNT (TV channel)">
       TNT
      </a>
      , a diverse group of artists paid him tribute, including Dylan,
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_Isaak" title="Chris Isaak">
       Chris Isaak
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">
       Wyclef Jean
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Norah_Jones" title="Norah Jones">
       Norah Jones
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">
       Kris Kristofferson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">
       Willie Nelson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dom_DeLuise" title="Dom DeLuise">
       Dom DeLuise
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">
       U2
      </a>
      . Cash himself appeared at the end and performed for the first time in more than a year. Two tribute albums were released shortly before his death;
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kindred_Spirits:_A_Tribute_to_the_Songs_of_Johnny_Cash" title="Kindred Spirits: A Tribute to the Songs of Johnny Cash">
        Kindred Spirits
       </a>
      </i>
      contains works from established artists, while
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dressed_in_Black:_A_Tribute_to_Johnny_Cash" title="Dressed in Black: A Tribute to Johnny Cash">
        Dressed in Black
       </a>
      </i>
      contains works from many lesser-known artists. In total, he wrote over 1,000 songs and released dozens of albums. A
      <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">
       box set
      </a>
      titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Unearthed_(Johnny_Cash_album)" title="Unearthed (Johnny Cash album)">
        Unearthed
       </a>
      </i>
      was issued posthumously. It included four CDs of unreleased material recorded with Rubin as well as a
      <i>
       Best of Cash on American
      </i>
      retrospective CD.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In recognition of his lifelong support of
      <a href="/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages" title="SOS Children's Villages">
       SOS Children's Villages
      </a>
      , his family invited friends and fans to donate to the Johnny Cash Memorial Fund in his memory. He had a personal link with the SOS village in
      <a href="/wiki/Die%C3%9Fen_am_Ammersee" title="Dieen am Ammersee">
       Diessen
      </a>
      , at the
      <a href="/wiki/Ammersee" title="Ammersee">
       Ammersee
      </a>
      Lake in
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_Germany" title="Southern Germany">
       Southern Germany
      </a>
      , near where he was stationed as a
      <a href="/wiki/G.I._(military)" title="G.I. (military)">
       G.I
      </a>
      , and with the SOS village in Barrett Town, by
      <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">
       Montego Bay
      </a>
      , near his holiday home in
      <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
       Jamaica
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1999, Cash received the
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">
       Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award
      </a>
      . In 2004,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      ranked Cash No. 31 on their "100 Greatest Artists of All Time" list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The main street in
      <a href="/wiki/Hendersonville,_Tennessee" title="Hendersonville, Tennessee">
       Hendersonville, Tennessee
      </a>
      , Highway 31E, is known as "Johnny Cash Parkway".
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <b>
       Johnny Cash Museum
      </b>
      was located in one of Cash's properties in Hendersonville dubbed the
      <i>
       House of Cash
      </i>
      until 2006 when it was sold based on the will of Cash. Prior to this, having been closed for a number of years, the museum had been featured in Cash's music video for "Hurt". The House subsequently burned down during the renovation by the new owner. A new Museum opened in 2013 in downtown Nashville.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 24, 2007, the Johnny Cash Flower Pickin' Festival was held in
      <a href="/wiki/Starkville,_Mississippi" title="Starkville, Mississippi">
       Starkville, Mississippi
      </a>
      , where Cash had been arrested more than 40 years earlier and held overnight at the city jail on May 11, 1965. The incident inspired Cash to write the song "Starkville City Jail". The festival, where he was offered a symbolic posthumous pardon, honored Cash's life and music, and was expected to become an annual event.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      JC Unit One, Johnny Cash's private tour bus from 1980 until 2003, was put on exhibit at the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">
       Rock and Roll Hall of Fame
      </a>
      and Museum in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">
       Cleveland, Ohio
      </a>
      , in 2007. The museum offers public tours of the bus on a seasonal basis (it is stored during the winter months and not exhibited during those times).
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Special_edition" title="Special edition">
       limited-edition
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forever_stamp" title="Forever stamp">
       Forever stamp
      </a>
      honoring Cash went on sale June 5, 2013. The stamp features a promotional picture of Cash taken around the 1963 release of "
      <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire:_The_Best_of_Johnny_Cash" title="Ring of Fire: The Best of Johnny Cash">
       Ring of Fire: The Best of Johnny Cash
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Portrayals">
       Portrayals
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Portrayals">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Country singer
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Collie" title="Mark Collie">
       Mark Collie
      </a>
      portrayed Cash in
      <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_Miller" title="John Lloyd Miller">
       John Lloyd Miller
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_Miller#Awards" title="John Lloyd Miller">
       award-winning
      </a>
      1999 short film,
      <i>
       I Still Miss Someone
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In November 2005,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Walk_the_Line" title="Walk the Line">
        Walk the Line
       </a>
      </i>
      , a biographical film about Cash's life, was released in the United States to considerable commercial success and critical acclaim. The film featured
      <a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Phoenix" title="Joaquin Phoenix">
       Joaquin Phoenix
      </a>
      as Johnny (for which he was nominated for the
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Actor">
       Academy Award for Best Actor
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Reese_Witherspoon" title="Reese Witherspoon">
       Reese Witherspoon
      </a>
      as June (for which she won the
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">
       Academy Award for Best Actress
      </a>
      ). Phoenix and Witherspoon also won the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" title="Golden Globe">
       Golden Globe
      </a>
      for Best Actor in a Musical or Comedy and Best Actress in a Musical or Comedy, respectively. They both performed their own vocals in the film (with their version of "Jackson" being released as a single), and Phoenix learned to play guitar for the role. Phoenix received a
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      for his contributions to the soundtrack. John Carter Cash, the son of Johnny and June, served as an executive producer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_69-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-imdb-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 12, 2006,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire_(musical)" title="Ring of Fire (musical)">
        Ring of Fire
       </a>
      </i>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Jukebox_musical" title="Jukebox musical">
       jukebox musical
      </a>
      of the Cash oeuvre, debuted on Broadway at the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethel_Barrymore_Theatre" title="Ethel Barrymore Theatre">
       Ethel Barrymore Theatre
      </a>
      , but closed due to harsh reviews and disappointing sales on April 30.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Quartet_(musical)" title="Million Dollar Quartet (musical)">
        Million Dollar Quartet
       </a>
      </i>
      , a musical portraying the early Sun recording sessions involving Cash, Elvis Presley, Jerry Lee Lewis, and Carl Perkins, debuted on Broadway on April 11, 2010. Actor
      <a href="/wiki/Lance_Guest" title="Lance Guest">
       Lance Guest
      </a>
      portrayed Cash. The musical was nominated for three awards at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Tony_Awards" title="2010 Tony Awards">
       2010 Tony Awards
      </a>
      , and won one.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hilburn" title="Robert Hilburn">
       Robert Hilburn
      </a>
      , veteran
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">
        Los Angeles Times
       </a>
      </i>
      pop music critic, the journalist who accompanied Cash in his 1968 Folsom prison tour and interviewed Cash many times throughout his life including months before his death, published a 688-page biography with 16 pages of photographs in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Cash_biography_118-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Cash_biography-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The meticulously reported biography is said to have filled in the 80 percent of Cash's life that was unknown, including details about Cash's battles with addiction and infidelity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Cash.27:_Meticulous_Attention_to_Facts_Sets_Robert_Hilburn.27s_Biography_Apart_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Cash.27:_Meticulous_Attention_to_Facts_Sets_Robert_Hilburn.27s_Biography_Apart-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The book reportedly does not hold back any details about the darker side of Johnny Cash and includes details about his affair with his pregnant wife June Carter's sister.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">
       Awards and honors
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <i>
        For detailed lists of music awards, see
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_received_by_Johnny_Cash" title="List of awards received by Johnny Cash">
         List of awards received by Johnny Cash
        </a>
        .
       </i>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      Cash received multiple
      <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">
       Country Music Association Awards
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">
       Grammys
      </a>
      , and other awards, in categories ranging from vocal and spoken performances to album notes and videos. In a career that spanned almost five decades during which he rose to recording industry icon status, Cash was the personification of country music to many people around the world. Cash was a musician who was not tied to a single genre. He recorded songs that could be considered
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">
       rock and roll
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">
       blues
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly">
       rockabilly
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">
       folk
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">
       gospel
      </a>
      , and exerted an influence on each of those genres. Moreover, he had the unique distinction among country artists of having "crossed over" late in his career to become popular with an unexpected audience, young
      <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">
       indie
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">
       alternative rock
      </a>
      fans.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      His diversity was evidenced by his presence in three major music halls of fame: the
      <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Nashville Songwriters Hall of Fame">
       Nashville Songwriters Hall of Fame
      </a>
      (1977), the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Country Music Hall of Fame">
       Country Music Hall of Fame
      </a>
      (1980), and the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">
       Rock and Roll Hall of Fame
      </a>
      (1992). Only thirteen performers are in both of the last two, and only
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hank_Williams_Sr." title="Hank Williams Sr.">
       Hank Williams Sr.
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Rodgers_(country_singer)" title="Jimmie Rodgers (country singer)">
       Jimmie Rodgers
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wills" title="Bob Wills">
       Bob Wills
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Monroe" title="Bill Monroe">
       Bill Monroe
      </a>
      share the honor with Cash of being in all three. Cash was the only inductee to the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame in the regular manner, unlike the other country members, who were inducted as "early influences".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      His contributions to the genre have been recognized by the
      <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rockabilly Hall of Fame">
       Rockabilly Hall of Fame
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cash received the
      <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">
       Kennedy Center Honors
      </a>
      in 1996, and stated that his induction into the Country Music Hall of Fame in 1980 was his greatest professional achievement. In 2001, he was awarded the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" title="National Medal of Arts">
       National Medal of Arts
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Hurt" was nominated for six VMAs at the 2003 MTV Video Music Awards. The only VMA the video won was that for Best Cinematography. With the video, Johnny Cash became the oldest artist ever nominated for an MTV Video Music Award.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">
       Justin Timberlake
      </a>
      , who won Best Video that year for "
      <a href="/wiki/Cry_Me_a_River_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Cry Me a River (Justin Timberlake song)">
       Cry Me a River
      </a>
      ", said in his acceptance speech: "This is a travesty! I demand a recount. My grandfather raised me on Johnny Cash, and I think he deserves this more than any of us in here tonight."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
       Notes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnny_Cash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-5">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-5">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although Cash's
         <a href="/wiki/Voice_type" title="Voice type">
          voice type
         </a>
         endured over the years, his
         <a href="/wiki/Timbre" title="Timbre">
          timbre
         </a>
         changed noticeably: "Through a recording career that stretche[d] back to 1955", Pareles writes, Cash's "bass-baritone voice [went] from gravelly to grave".
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPareles1994_4-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPareles1994-4">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           4
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-12">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-12">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         For Cash, black stage attire was a "symbol of rebellionagainst a stagnant status quo, against... hypocritical houses of God, against people whose minds are closed to others' ideas".
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DJPbbxoWZdSwC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_64.5D_11-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr2003.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DJPbbxoWZdSwC.26printsec.3Dfrontcover.26source.3Dgbs_navlinks_s.23v.3Donepage.26q.3D.26f.3Dfalse_64.5D-11">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           10
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-14">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-14">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Schultz refers to this phrase as Cash's "trademark greeting", and places his utterance of this line, on Cash's
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/At_Folsom_Prison" title="At Folsom Prison">
           At Folsom Prison
          </a>
         </i>
         album, "among the most electrifying [seconds] in the history of concert recording."
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schultz_13-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Schultz-13">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           11
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-91">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-91">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Other appraisals of Cash's iconic value have been even bolder.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClapp2008xvi_90-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClapp2008xvi-90">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           87
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Urbanski_black-104">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Urbanski_black_104-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Urbanski
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrbanski200339_101-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbanski200339-101">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           97
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         notes that Cash's habit of performing in black attire began in a church. In the following paragraph, he
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrbanski200339.E2.80.9340_102-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrbanski200339.E2.80.9340-102">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           98
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         quotes Cash
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashCarr200364_103-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashCarr200364-103">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           99
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         as indicating that this habit was partially reflective of Cash's rebellion "against our hypocritical houses of God".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Urbanski2-106">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Urbanski2_106-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         According to Urbanski, Cash's self-perception was accurate: "He never intended to be categorized or pigeonholed", and indeed he amassed a "cluster of enigmas" which "was so impenetrably deep that even those closest to him never got to see every part of him".
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
          <a href="#cite_note-105">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           100
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">

      </span>

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
